<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of the United Kingdom.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/48px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/64px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:United_Kingdom" title="Portal:United Kingdom">United Kingdom&#32;portal</a>  <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Brief_history_and_overview">Brief history and overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Brief history and overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Before the mid-19th century, <a href="/wiki/Politics_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Politics in the United Kingdom">politics in the United Kingdom</a> was dominated by the <a href="/wiki/British_Whig_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="British Whig Party">Whigs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Tory_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="British Tory Party">Tories</a>. These were not political parties in the modern sense but somewhat loose alliances of interests and individuals. The Whigs included many of the leading aristocratic dynasties committed to the Protestant succession, and later drew support from elements of the emerging industrial interests and wealthy  merchants, while the Tories were associated with the <a href="/wiki/Landed_gentry" title="Landed gentry">landed gentry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a>.
</p><p>By the mid 19th century, the Tories had evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>, and the Whigs had evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal Party</a>. The parliament was presided over by a speaker, who handled proceedings. The concept of right and left came originally from France, where the Right supported a smaller state with less influence on the lives of the public, the Left advocated a larger state with more influence on the lives of the public. In the late 19th century the Liberal Party began to lean towards the left, and the seating in the house of commons began to reflect this: Right of the speaker were those supporting right wing politics, the Conservatives; left of the speaker were those supporting Left wing politics, the Liberals. <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Unionist_Party" title="Liberal Unionist Party">Liberal Unionists</a> split off from the Liberals over <a href="/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule_movement" title="Irish Home Rule movement">Irish Home Rule</a> and moved closer to the Conservatives over time.
</p><p>The Liberals and Conservatives dominated the political scene until the 1920s, when the Liberal Party declined in popularity and suffered a long stream of resignations. It was replaced as the main anti-Tory opposition party by the newly emerging <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>, which represented an alliance between the <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">labour movement</a>, organised <a href="/wiki/Trade_unions_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Trade unions in the United Kingdom">trades unions</a> and various <a href="/wiki/Socialist_society_(Labour_Party)" title="Socialist society (Labour Party)">socialist societies</a>.
</p><p>Since then the Conservative and Labour parties have dominated British politics, and have alternated in government ever since. However, the UK is not quite a two-party system as other parties have significant support. The <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> were the third largest party until the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a> when they were overtaken by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> in terms of seats and UK political party membership, and by the <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UK Independence Party</a> in terms of votes.
</p><p>The UK's <a href="/wiki/First_Past_the_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="First Past the Post">First Past the Post</a> electoral system leaves small parties disadvantaged on a UK-wide scale. It can, however, allow parties with concentrations of supporters in the <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">constituent countries</a> to flourish. In the 2015 election there was widespread controversy<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> when <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UKIP</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party of England and Wales</a> received 4.9 million votes<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> (12.6% of the total vote for UKIP and 3.8% for the Greens) yet only gained one seat each in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>. After that election, UKIP, the Liberal Democrats, and the Green Party of England and Wales, together with its Scottish and Northern Ireland affiliated parties, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru" title="Plaid Cymru">Plaid Cymru</a>, delivered a petition signed by 477,000<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> people to <a href="/wiki/Downing_Street" title="Downing Street">Downing Street</a> demanding <a href="/wiki/Electoral_reform" title="Electoral reform">electoral reform</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debating_chamber,_Scottish_Parliament_(31-05-2006).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg/220px-Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg/330px-Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg/440px-Debating_chamber%2C_Scottish_Parliament_%2831-05-2006%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1587" data-file-height="1161" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Debating_chamber,_Scottish_Parliament_(31-05-2006).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> debating chamber</div></div></div><p> Since 1997, <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>-based voting systems have been adopted for elections to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a>, the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a> and the UK's seats in the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>. In these bodies, other parties have had success.
</p><p>Traditionally political parties have been private organisations with no official recognition by the state. The <a href="/wiki/Registration_of_Political_Parties_Act_1998" title="Registration of Political Parties Act 1998">Registration of Political Parties Act 1998</a> changed that by creating a register of parties.
</p><p>Membership of political parties has been in decline in the UK since the 1950s, falling by over 65% from 1983 (4% of the electorate) to 2005 (1.3%).<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_start_of_political_parties">The start of political parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The start of political parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_Kingdom)" title="Electoral Commission (United Kingdom)">Electoral Commission's</a> Register of Political Parties<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> lists the details of parties registered to fight elections in the United Kingdom, including their registered name. Under current electoral law, including the Registration of Political Parties Act, the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Administration_Act_2006" title="Electoral Administration Act 2006">Electoral Administration Act 2006</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Political_Parties,_Elections_and_Referendums_Act_2000" title="Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000">Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000</a>, only registered party names can be used on ballot papers by those wishing to fight elections. Candidates who do not belong to a registered party can use "independent" or no label at all.
</p><p>As of  3&#160;August&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the Electoral Commission showed the number of registered political parties in Great Britain and Northern Ireland as 492.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_Parties">Parliamentary Parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Parliamentary Parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Two parties dominate politics in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom House of Commons">House of Commons</a>. Each one operates throughout <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> (only the Conservative and Unionist Party stands candidates in Northern Ireland). Most of the British <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a> represent one of these parties:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative and Unionist Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Centre-right" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-right">centre-right</a> (316 seats in the House of Commons)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>, (257 seats)
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Co-operative_Party" title="Co-operative Party">Co-operative Party</a> (all Co-operative Party MPs are also Labour MPs as part of a long-standing electoral agreement)</li></ul></li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Party_descriptions">Party descriptions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Party descriptions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr bgcolor="#cccccc">
<th colspan="2" scope="col" width="5px">Party
</th>
<th scope="col">Description
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #0087DC">
</th>
<td style="width: 100pt;"><a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative and Unionist Party</a>
</td>
<td>A party loosely divided into three categories: The <a href="/wiki/Thatcherism" title="Thatcherism">Thatcherites</a> or <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Way_Forward" title="Conservative Way Forward">Conservative Way Forward</a>, who strongly support a free market and tend to be <a href="/wiki/Euroscepticism" title="Euroscepticism">Eurosceptic</a>; the economically moderate, often more pro-European and socially liberal <a href="/wiki/One_Nation_Conservatism" class="mw-redirect" title="One Nation Conservatism">One Nation Conservatives</a>, and the socially conservative, deeply Eurosceptic <a href="/wiki/Cornerstone_Group" title="Cornerstone Group">Cornerstone Group</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #DC241f">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>
</td>
<td>A <a href="/wiki/Big_tent" title="Big tent">big tent</a> party, broadly centre-left with roots in the <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade union</a> movement.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #FEF987">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Scottish_nationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish nationalist">Scottish nationalist</a> and social democratic party which supports of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Independence">Scottish Independence</a> and membership of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #FAA61A">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">Liberal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">social liberal</a>. The party's main two branches are the social-liberal grouping, and the '<a href="/wiki/The_Orange_Book:_Reclaiming_Liberalism" title="The Orange Book: Reclaiming Liberalism">Orange Book</a>' grouping, which supports classical <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">economic liberalism</a>. Strongly supports membership of the European Union.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #D46A4C">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Unionist_Party" title="Democratic Unionist Party">Democratic Unionist Party</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Unionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Unionism in the United Kingdom">Unionist</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_conservatism" title="National conservatism">national conservative</a> party in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. <a href="/wiki/Social_conservatism" title="Social conservatism">Socially conservative</a> with close links to <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #008800">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn Féin">Sinn Féin</a> <sup>†</sup>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Irish_republicanism" title="Irish republicanism">Irish republican</a> party that supports the unification of the island of Ireland as a 32-county Irish republic.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #008142">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Plaid_Cymru_-_Party_of_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaid Cymru - Party of Wales">Plaid Cymru - Party of Wales</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Social-democratic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_nationalism" title="Welsh nationalism">Welsh nationalist</a> party in favour of <a href="/wiki/Welsh_independence" title="Welsh independence">Welsh independence</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #99FF66">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_and_Labour_Party" title="Social Democratic and Labour Party">Social Democratic and Labour Party</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Social-democratic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">Irish nationalist</a> party supporting a <a href="/wiki/United_Ireland" title="United Ireland">United Ireland</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #9999FF">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ulster_Unionist_Party" title="Ulster Unionist Party">Ulster Unionist Party</a>
</td>
<td>Unionist party in Northern Ireland, <a href="/wiki/Conservative" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative">conservative</a> but with liberal factions.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #6AB023">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party of England and Wales</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green political</a> party that favours <a href="/wiki/Eco-socialism" title="Eco-socialism">eco-socialism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Green_Party_core_values_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Green_Party_core_values-23">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Green_Party_core_values_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Green_Party_core_values-23">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a><sup id="cite_ref-Green_Party_core_values_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Green_Party_core_values-23">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Non-violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violence">non-violence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Green_Party_core_values_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Green_Party_core_values-23">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #70147A">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UK Independence Party</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Euroscepticism" title="Euroscepticism">Eurosceptic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_populism" title="Right-wing populism">right-wing populist</a> party. Favours national sovereignty, <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_conservatism" title="Social conservatism">social conservatism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">economic liberalism</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #F6CB2F">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Alliance_Party_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Alliance Party of Northern Ireland">Alliance Party of Northern Ireland</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">Liberal</a> and centrist political party in Northern Ireland.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #62A439">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Green_Party" title="Scottish Green Party">Scottish Green Party</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green political</a> party in favour of <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">Scottish independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_republicanism" title="Scottish republicanism">Scottish republicanism</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #8dc63f">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Green_Party_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Green Party in Northern Ireland">Green Party in Northern Ireland</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green political</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nonsectarian" title="Nonsectarian">nonsectarian</a> party in Northern Ireland.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #0095B6">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Traditional_Unionist_Voice" title="Traditional Unionist Voice">Traditional Unionist Voice</a>
</td>
<td>Strongly social and national conservative unionist party in Northern Ireland, opposed to the <a href="/wiki/St_Andrews_Agreement" title="St Andrews Agreement">St Andrews Agreement</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th style="background-color: #660000">
</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/People_Before_Profit" title="People Before Profit">People Before Profit</a>
</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">Socialist</a> party.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>† Sinn Féin MPs do not take their seats in the UK House of Commons as they refuse to swear allegiance to the Crown, nor recognise Westminster's right to legislate for any part of Ireland.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="No_elected_representation">No elected representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: No elected representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(February 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This is a list of <a href="/wiki/Notability_in_the_English_Wikipedia" title="Notability in the English Wikipedia">notable</a> minor parties. Many parties are registered with the Electoral Commission but do not qualify for this list as they have not received significant independent coverage.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_English_parties">Minor English parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Minor English parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_England" title="Politics of England">Politics of England</a></div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_London" title="List of political parties in London">List of political parties in London</a></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Community_Action_Party" title="Community Action Party">Community Action Party</a>; local centre-left party in <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Wigan" title="Metropolitan Borough of Wigan">Wigan</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Community_Group" title="Community Group">Community Group</a>; local party in <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/English_Democrats" title="English Democrats">English Democrats</a>; campaign for <a href="/wiki/Self-government" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-government">self-government</a> for <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Health_Action_Party" title="National Health Action Party">National Health Action Party</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Party_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Democratic Party (UK)">People's Democratic Party</a>, a populist party focused on Northern England.</li>
<li>The Republic Party, based in <a href="/wiki/Pendlebury_(ward)" title="Pendlebury (ward)">Pendlebury</a>, Salford. Campaigning for the UK to become a Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Party" title="Roman Party">Roman Party</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wessex_Regionalist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Wessex Regionalist Party">Wessex Regionalist Party</a>, campaigning for devolution for <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Wessex</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_Scottish_parties">Minor Scottish parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Minor Scottish parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li><a href="/wiki/RISE_%E2%80%93_Scotland%27s_Left_Alliance" title="RISE – Scotland&#39;s Left Alliance">RISE – Scotland's Left Alliance</a>; electoral alliance formed by <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Socialist_Party" title="Scottish Socialist Party">SSP</a> and former <a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Group_(Scotland)" title="International Socialist Group (Scotland)">ISG</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Libertarian_Party" title="Scottish Libertarian Party">Scottish Libertarian Party</a>, a libertarian, pro-independence and Eurosceptic party</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Senior_Citizens_Unity_Party" title="Scottish Senior Citizens Unity Party">Scottish Senior Citizens Unity Party</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Socialist_Party" title="Scottish Socialist Party">Scottish Socialist Party</a>, a party campaigning for an independent, socialist and republican Scotland.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Unionist_Party_(modern)" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Unionist Party (modern)">Scottish Unionist Party</a>, campaigns to prevent dissolution of the <a href="/wiki/UK" class="mw-redirect" title="UK">UK</a>. Has strong links with the <a href="/wiki/Orange_Order" title="Orange Order">Orange Order</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_Scotland" title="Socialist Party Scotland">Socialist Party Scotland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Scotland)" title="Solidarity (Scotland)">Solidarity</a>, a split from the SSP in 2006.</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Defunct_and_historical_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom">Defunct and historical parties in the United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Defunct and historical parties in the United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Social_Democracy" title="Campaign for Social Democracy">Campaign for Social Democracy</a> (1973–1974)</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Respect_Party" title="Respect Party">Respect Party</a> (2004-2016)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Science_Party_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Science Party (UK)">Science Party</a>. Launched in April 2010, with initial press support from Newscientist.com. Campaigning for increased importance and use of Science in Politics.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Social_Credit_Party_of_Great_Britain_and_Northern_Ireland" title="Social Credit Party of Great Britain and Northern Ireland">Social Credit Party of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</a> (1931–1951, 1965–1978)</li>
